<p><i><b>Take Me Home</b></i> is the second studio album by <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British</a>-<a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> group <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a>, released on 9 November 2012 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony Music Entertainment</a>. As a follow-up to One Direction's internationally successful debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(One_Direction_album)" title="Up All Night (One Direction album)">Up All Night</a></i> (2011), <i>Take Me Home</i> was written in groups and has an average of just under five songwriters per track. Largely recorded and composed in Sweden during 2012, <a href="/wiki/Savan_Kotecha" title="Savan Kotecha">Savan Kotecha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rami_Yacoub" title="Rami Yacoub">Rami Yacoub</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Falk" title="Carl Falk">Carl Falk</a>, who composed One Direction's hits, "<a href="/wiki/What_Makes_You_Beautiful" title="What Makes You Beautiful">What Makes You Beautiful</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/One_Thing_(One_Direction_song)" title="One Thing (One Direction song)">One Thing</a>", spent six months in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> developing songs for the album, and were able to shape <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melodies</a> around the members' tones.</p>
<p>The album's songs are characterised by <a href="/wiki/Metronome" title="Metronome">metronomic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pop_(music)" title="Pop (music)">pop</a>, vocal harmonies, hand claps, prominent electric guitar riffs, bright synthesizers, a <a href="/wiki/Homogeneity_and_heterogeneity" title="Homogeneity and heterogeneity">homogeneous</a> sound and message, and rotations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lead_vocal" title="Lead vocal">lead vocals</a>. The members' voices are presented individually on the record, and its lyricism speaks of falling in love, <a href="/wiki/Unrequited_love" title="Unrequited love">unrequited love</a>, the insistence that flaws are what make a person unique, commitment, jealousy, and longing for past significant others. <i>Take Me Home</i> garnered mostly positive reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. There was praise for its quality of production, while criticism hinged on its generic, rushed nature.</p>
<p>Globally, the album topped the charts in more than 35 countries, and was the fourth best-selling album of 2012, selling 12.4 million units. The album's number-one debut on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart made One Direction the first group to bow atop the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with their first two albums since American girl group <a href="/wiki/Danity_Kane" title="Danity Kane">Danity Kane</a> entered with <i><a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Dollhouse_(album)" title="Welcome to the Dollhouse (album)">Welcome to the Dollhouse</a></i> in 2008 and their <a href="/wiki/Danity_Kane_(album)" title="Danity Kane (album)">self-titled debut</a> in 2006. One Direction also became the second act in 2012 to achieve two number-one albums within a 12-month period, and the first boy band in US chart history to land two number-one albums in a calendar year. Their debut album and <i>Take Me Home</i> were the third and fifth best-selling albums of 2012 in the United States, respectively, making the band the first act to place two albums in the year-end top five in the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> era.</p>
<p>The album's lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Live_While_We%27re_Young" title="Live While We're Young">Live While We're Young</a>", released on 28 September 2012, peaked inside the top ten in almost every country it charted in and recorded the highest one-week opening sales figure for a song by a non-US artist. The subsequent singles, "<a href="/wiki/Little_Things_(One_Direction_song)" title="Little Things (One Direction song)">Little Things</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Kiss_You_(One_Direction_song)" title="Kiss You (One Direction song)">Kiss You</a>", were less successful, although the former topped the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>. To support the release, One Direction performed the album's songs on several televised programmes and during their worldwide <i><a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Home_Tour_(One_Direction)" title="Take Me Home Tour (One Direction)">Take Me Home Tour</a></i> (2013). This is when Larry Stylinson (the relationship between band members Harry Styles and Louis Tomlinson) was made official.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_production">Background and production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take_Me_Home_(One_Direction_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background and production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="574" data-file-width="794" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg/200px-One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg/300px-One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg/400px-One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:One_Direction_2012_Stockholm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One Direction greet Swedish fans in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, May 2012, as the recording commenced at Kinglet Studios.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2012, One Direction revealed that a follow-up release to their debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_(One_Direction_album)" title="Up All Night (One Direction album)">Up All Night</a></i> (2011), was in development. "In the summer, we're going to get back and start a new record. We want to bring out a record nearly every year, every year and a half," <a href="/wiki/Niall_Horan" title="Niall Horan">Niall Horan</a> said, revealing they were arranging "meetings and stuff with different writers and producers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalpost1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-nationalpost1-1">[1]</a></sup> In March 2012, <a href="/wiki/McFly" title="McFly">McFly</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Tom_Fletcher" title="Tom Fletcher">Tom Fletcher</a> confirmed that he would be writing a song for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In February 2012, One Direction expressed interest in working with <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and in June 2012, Sheeran confirmed that they were in contact: "I'm going into the studio in August to produce the tracks for them. I won't feature on the tracks though".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>, the group's manager, had challenged prominent songwriters to compete for space on One Direction's second album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ide_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-ide-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dee_Demirbag" title="Dee Demirbag">Dee Demirbag</a>, responsible for repertoire at <a href="/wiki/BMG_Rights_Management" title="BMG Rights Management">BMG Rights Management</a>, a music publisher, in Scandinavia, said: "Breaking a boy band in the U.S. is about as big as it gets in the music industry, so you can imagine the competition to get cuts on the next One Direction album is immense".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ide_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-ide-5">[5]</a></sup> In addition, the article reported that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syco_Records" title="Syco Records">Syco Records</a> was working on candidates with <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kristian_Lundin" title="Kristian Lundin">Kristian Lundin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ide_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-ide-5">[5]</a></sup> By August 2012, it was confirmed that album would feature work from veterans such as <a href="/wiki/Carl_Falk" title="Carl Falk">Carl Falk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rami_Yacoub" title="Rami Yacoub">Rami Yacoub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Luke" title="Dr. Luke">Dr. Luke</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cirkut_(producer)" title="Cirkut (producer)">Cirkut</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shellback_(producer)" title="Shellback (producer)">Shellback</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard1-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Take Me Home</i> was written in groups and has an average of just under five songwriters per track. "The Swedish-style songwriting: melody first" was predominantly utilised, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> correspondent Douglas Wolk. <a href="/wiki/Savan_Kotecha" title="Savan Kotecha">Savan Kotecha</a>, Yacoub, and Falk, who composed One Direction's hits, "<a href="/wiki/What_Makes_You_Beautiful" title="What Makes You Beautiful">What Makes You Beautiful</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/One_Thing_(One_Direction_song)" title="One Thing (One Direction song)">One Thing</a>", spent six months in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, developing songs for the album, and were able to shape melodies around their tones. Kotecha reflected: "We’ll spend days, sometimes weeks, challenging the melody. The goal is to make it sound like anyone can do this, but it's actually very difficult".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup> In addition, after viewing the international success of "What Makes You Beautiful", the trio conceptualised songs "that kids could play on guitar and cover on YouTube."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>After extensive promotional appearances in support of their debut album, One Direction began recording the album in May 2012, in Stockholm, Sweden, at Kinglet Studios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-credits_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-credits-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In June 2012, the group continued recording the album in the United States, while touring on the final leg of their <i><a href="/wiki/Up_All_Night_Tour" title="Up All Night Tour">Up All Night Tour</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CapitalFM_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-CapitalFM-11">[11]</a></sup> Horan, in a June interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a>, disclosed that the group were intending to spend their time in July and August "getting the album done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Besides sessions in Kinglet Studios, recording sessions and mixing for the album took place at Chalice Studios in Los Angeles, MixStar Studios in Virginia Beach, Wendy House Productions in London, and Sticky Studios in Surrey, England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-credits_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-credits-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Packaging">Packaging</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take_Me_Home_(One_Direction_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Packaging">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The album cover artwork, revealed on 30 August 2012, features the group surrounding a traditional British K2 <a href="/wiki/Red_telephone_box" title="Red telephone box">red telephone box</a>, a familiar sight on the streets of the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_lyrics">Music and lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take_Me_Home_(One_Direction_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Music and lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="468" data-file-width="800" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg/210px-Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg/315px-Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg/420px-Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clash_21051980_12_800.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The opening guitar riff of "<a href="/wiki/Live_While_We%27re_Young" title="Live While We're Young">Live While We're Young</a>" was compared by some critics to that of <a href="/wiki/The_Clash" title="The Clash">The Clash</a>'s (<i>pictured</i>) 1982 single, "<a href="/wiki/Should_I_Stay_or_Should_I_Go" title="Should I Stay or Should I Go">Should I Stay or Should I Go</a>".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The album's songs are characterised by <a href="/wiki/Metronome" title="Metronome">metronomic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_(music)" title="Rock (music)">rock</a>-inherited <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pop_(music)" title="Pop (music)">pop</a>, vocal harmonies, hand claps, prominent electric guitar riffs, bright synthesizers, <a href="/wiki/Double_entendre" title="Double entendre">double entendres</a> for <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Homogeneity_and_heterogeneity" title="Homogeneity and heterogeneity">homogeneous</a> sound and message, the pitch-correcting software <a href="/wiki/Auto-Tune" title="Auto-Tune">Auto-Tune</a>, and rotations of lead vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZH_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-NZH-18">[18]</a></sup> Jon Caramanica, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, considered the album "far more mechanical" than their debut album, although noted that it is sonically and lyrically similar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-16">[16]</a></sup> San Lansky, an editor for <a href="/wiki/Idolator_(website)" title="Idolator (website)">Idolator</a>, described it as "’80s-inflected and intermittently rock-dappled," and as more indebted to the "sanitized <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a> crunch of McFly" than to <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idolator_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Idolator-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alexis_Petridis" title="Alexis Petridis">Alexis Petridis</a>, a music journalist, interpreted its signature sound as a "peppy, synth-bolstered take on early-80s <a href="/wiki/New_wave_music" title="New wave music">new-wave</a> pop, heavy on clipped rhythms and chugging guitars," which, he said, is at least an improvement on the substitute <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> "that was once the grim lot of the boyband."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-17">[17]</a></sup> The opening <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guitar_riff" title="Guitar riff">guitar riff</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Live_While_We%27re_Young" title="Live While We're Young">Live While We're Young</a>" has been noted as similar to that of <a href="/wiki/The_Clash" title="The Clash">The Clash</a>'s 1982 single, "<a href="/wiki/Should_I_Stay_or_Should_I_Go" title="Should I Stay or Should I Go">Should I Stay or Should I Go</a>", by some critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZH_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-NZH-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fix_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-fix-20">[20]</a></sup> According to Petridis, the guitar is played thrice between the riff with the plectrum stroking the strings, while it is pressed. One note in the chord is changed, which Petridis surmised was probably to avoid paying any royalty to the Clash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-17">[17]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Rock_Me_(One_Direction_song)" title="Rock Me (One Direction song)">Rock Me</a>" has a clapping, mid-<a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> <a href="/wiki/Beat_(music)" title="Beat (music)">beat</a> that has been likened to that "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>", a 1977 single by <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hitfix_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hitfix-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The group's voices are presented individually on the record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup> Savan Kotecha noted that the <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a>' late-’90s hits inspired the way he formulated One Direction's voices for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-6"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup> Composer Julian Bunetta, who worked on three of <i>Take Me Home</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> tracks, also tried to place emphasis on the sound of each member: "The fans can tell the difference, but we wanted to make sure that when it came on the radio, the average person knew that it must be One Direction, because it’s five guys."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_7-7"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-7">[7]</a></sup> Likewise, Caramanica noted that the album's songs produced by Bunetta "tend to start out with more breathing room, giving the guys a chance to show off vocally". The album's lyricism speaks of falling in love, <a href="/wiki/Unrequited_love" title="Unrequited love">unrequited love</a>, the insistence that flaws are what make a person unique, and commitment, in songs such as "<a href="/wiki/Little_Things_(One_Direction_song)" title="Little Things (One Direction song)">Little Things</a>," "Last First Kiss," "Back For You," and "They Don't Know About Us."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZH_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-NZH-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyrics_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lyrics-22">[22]</a></sup> Other tracks, like "Heart Attack," "Rock Me," "I Would," and "Over Again," have a more solemn tone, addressing jealousy and longing for past significant others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyrics_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lyrics-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take_Me_Home_(One_Direction_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:226px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:One_Direction_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1977" data-file-width="3761" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/One_Direction_2013.jpg/224px-One_Direction_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/One_Direction_2013.jpg/336px-One_Direction_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/One_Direction_2013.jpg/448px-One_Direction_2013.jpg 2x" width="224"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:One_Direction_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One Direction performing in Glasgow during the album's <a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Home_Tour_(One_Direction)" title="Take Me Home Tour (One Direction)">accompanying concert tour</a>, February 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Take Me Home</i> has yielded three singles, including two US singles. Its lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Live_While_We%27re_Young" title="Live While We're Young">Live While We're Young</a>", was released by Syco Records on 28 September 2012. The song rocketed to worldwide success, peaking at number one in Ireland and New Zealand and the top ten in almost every country it charted in.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In the United States, "Live While We're Young" debuted at number three on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, sold 341,000 downloads in its first week, and bowed at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Digital_Songs" title="Digital Songs">Digital Songs</a> chart. Its debut marks the highest bow by a British group and the second-highest debut among all UK acts, outpaced only by <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s number one arrival with "<a href="/wiki/Candle_in_the_Wind_1997" title="Candle in the Wind 1997">Candle in the Wind 1997</a>". Its opening sales denote the biggest opening sales figure for a single by a non-US artist and the third ever for a download by a group, surpassed by the arrivals of <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>'s 2012 single, "<a href="/wiki/Payphone_(song)" title="Payphone (song)">Payphone</a>" (493,000), and <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a>' 2009 single, "<a href="/wiki/Boom_Boom_Pow" title="Boom Boom Pow">Boom Boom Pow</a>" (465,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboarddebut_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboarddebut-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Musicweek1_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Musicweek1-27">[27]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Little_Things_(One_Direction_song)" title="Little Things (One Direction song)">Little Things</a>" was released in the UK and Ireland on 12 November 2012, as the second single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lout_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-lout-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVNEWS_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNEWS-29">[29]</a></sup> The track debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> of 18 November 2012, becoming One Direction's fifth top ten appearance and second number-one hit in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKdebut_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKdebut-30">[30]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Kiss_You_(One_Direction_song)" title="Kiss You (One Direction song)">Kiss You</a>", chosen as the second and final US single third and final overall single of <i>Take Me Home</i>, was released <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digitally</a> on 17 November 2012, according to MTV News.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVNEWS2_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNEWS2-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The group and the album's lead single were featured in a <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> television commercial for the United States, which premiered on the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox Broadcasting Company</a> network on 10 October 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pepsi_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pepsi-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> allowed the record to stream in full on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> in the week leading up to its 13 November 2012 release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In addition, One Direction promoted the album in a series of live appearances from October toward December, notably on television programmes <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S.)" title="The X Factor (U.S.)">The X Factor USA</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor UK</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Today_(U.S._TV_program)" title="Today (U.S. TV program)">The Today Show</a></i>, which drew a record crowd of 15.000 people to the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Children_in_Need_2012" title="Children in Need 2012">Children in Need 2012</a></i> telethon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Additional live appearances include at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Variety_Performance" title="Royal Variety Performance">Royal Variety Performance</a>, in the presence of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bambi_Awards" title="Bambi Awards">Bambi Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and a headlining sold-out show at New York City's <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The album's accompanying concert tour, the <i><a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Home_Tour_(One_Direction)" title="Take Me Home Tour (One Direction)">Take Me Home Tour</a></i>, commenced at London's <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena" title="The O2 Arena">O2 Arena</a> on 23 February 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Capital_FM_Take_Me_Home_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Capital_FM_Take_Me_Home-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mirror_Take_Me_Home_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mirror_Take_Me_Home-42">[42]</a></sup> The concert tour consists of over 100 shows in Australasia, Europe, and North America, and is set to visit arenas and stadiums from February through October 2013. Announced by member <a href="/wiki/Liam_Payne" title="Liam Payne">Liam Payne</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_BRIT_Awards" title="2012 BRIT Awards">2012 BRIT Awards</a> in early 2012, the original concert tour was billed as the UK &amp; Ireland Arena Tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In mid-2012, the concert tour expanded with legs in North America and <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a> following the band's international breakthrough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In the UK and Ireland, ticket sales reached 300,000 within a day of release, which included a six-date sell out at the O2 Arena in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In Australian and New Zealand markets, tickets grossed US$15.7 million, with all 190,000 tickets being sold for eighteen shows to be held in Australia and New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take_Me_Home_(One_Direction_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle">favourable<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-57">[57]</a></sup></td>

</table>
<p>The album received generally positive reviews from contemporary <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalised</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream critics, the album received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">average</a> score of 68, based on ten reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-49">[49]</a></sup> Despite its "boardroom-defined objectives" and "safety", Al Fox, writing for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Music" title="BBC Music">BBC Music</a>, considered the music itself "notable quality" and reliable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCmusic_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBCmusic-50">[50]</a></sup> Matt Collar from <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">Allmusic</a> described it as an "immediately catchy mix of dancey pop that maximizes the group's shared lead-vocal approach and peppy, upbeat image."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-15">[15]</a></sup> Kate Wills from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> praised the uptempo material while defining the ballads as jarring, a notion shared by John Dolan of <i>Rolling Stone</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-RS-55">[55]</a></sup> Although he dubbed it "actually pretty great – certainly better than it needs to be," Sam Lansky for Idolator thought the album is predictably generic, and interpreted it as "a little cynical, even as it excels in making some of the purest pop of the year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idolator_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Idolator-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> writer Adam Markovitz panned the record as an empty gesture and asserted that the album was rushed, signifying an album with "barely enough zip to keep the kids up past dinner."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-EW-52">[52]</a></sup> Likewise, Robert Copsey from <i><a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a></i> wrote, "The result [of <i>Take Me Home</i>] may see them progressing at a snail's pace, but when you've got it so good, what's the rush anyway?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digital_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-digital-58">[58]</a></sup> In a mixed review, <i>The New York Times</i> contributor Jon Caramanica appreciated the album's sonic palette, but dismissed its lyricism as narrow and tedious, and Sheeran's contributions as "unusually lumpy in the hands of such a polished group". Caramanica characterised the members' vocals as "fundamentally interchangeable", and opined that only <a href="/wiki/Zayn_Malik" title="Zayn Malik">Zayn Malik</a> "breaks free from the pack vocally with any regularity."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>While he commended the album for its "variable quality", Alexis Petridis for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> felt the record would not be able to transcend its target market, a core audience aged approximately 8 to 12 and female: "To anyone else, the mystery of One Direction's success – or at least the sheer scale of it – remains as opaque as ever."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-17">[17]</a></sup> The latter view was shared by <a href="/wiki/Ben_Rayner" title="Ben Rayner">Ben Rayner</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Star" title="Toronto Star">Toronto Star</a></i>: "Unless you’re in the target demographic or are, perhaps, a mom who lived through the same thing in her youth, there's no point in even going near this record, of course, but the rest of us were never meant to in the first place."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Star_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Star-59">[59]</a></sup> Writing for <i><a href="/wiki/HitFix" title="HitFix">HitFix</a></i>, Melinda Newman maintained that the album "masterfully hits its target", and concluded as follows: "I’m so far out of the One Dimension demographic, I practically need a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">GPS</a> to find it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hitfix_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hitfix-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take_Me_Home_(One_Direction_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Globally, <i>Take Me Home</i> topped the charts in more than 35 countries, and was the fourth best-selling album of 2012, selling 4.4 million units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFPI_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-IFPI-61">[61]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, the album sold over 94,000 copies in its first two days of sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> It debuted atop the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> with first-week sales of 155,000 copies, becoming their first album to top the chart and the second fastest selling album of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKdebut_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-UKdebut-30">[30]</a></sup> The album and its second single, "<a href="/wiki/Little_Things_(One_Direction_song)" title="Little Things (One Direction song)">Little Things</a>", both debuted simultaneously at number one in the UK on 18 November 2012, making One Direction the youngest act in British chart history to achieve the feat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The album became the fifth best-selling album of 2012 in the UK, having sold 616,000 copies by the end of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKend_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKend-64">[64]</a></sup> It was certified double platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI) on 15 February 2013, denoting shipments of 600,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPI_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-65">[65]</a></sup> As of November 2014, the album has sold 960,255 copies in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sales_2014_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-sales_2014-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Ireland, <i>Take Me Home</i> became the fastest-selling album of 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> lodged six consecutive weeks atop the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Albums_Chart" title="Irish Albums Chart">Irish Albums Chart</a>, and was certified triple platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Recorded_Music_Association" title="Irish Recorded Music Association">Irish Recorded Music Association</a> (IRMA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Irelandcert_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Irelandcert-69">[69]</a></sup> In Italy, the collection became their second Italian chart-topper, and Italy's seventh best-selling album of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Italypeak_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Italypeak-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Italyyearend_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Italyyearend-71">[71]</a></sup> It has been certified double platinum by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_Italian_Music_Industry" title="Federation of the Italian Music Industry">Federation of the Italian Music Industry</a> (FIMI), indicating sales of 60,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Italycert_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Italycert-72">[72]</a></sup> In the Netherlands, the album debuted at number-one on 17 November 2012, and shipped 25,000 copies in its first day of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NLpeak_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-NLpeak-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollandcert_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hollandcert-74">[74]</a></sup> It was certified platinum by 18 December 2012, denoting shipments of 50,000 copies in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollandcert_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hollandcert-74">[74]</a></sup> After a month of its release, it was certified platinum in Poland for shipments of 30,000 copies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Polandcert_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Polandcert-75">[75]</a></sup> while it became the seventh best-selling album of 2012 in Denmark, having sold 28,875 copies by year end in that country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Danishyearend_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Danishyearend-76">[76]</a></sup> In Sweden, the album was the ninth best-selling album of 2012, and has been certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Swedish Recording Industry Association">Swedish Recording Industry Association</a> (GLF), signifying shipments of 40,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Swedencert_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Swedencert-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album debuted at number one on the Australian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARIA_Chart" title="ARIA Chart">ARIA Chart</a> dated 25 November 2012, a position it held for a second week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Australiapeak_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Australiapeak-78">[78]</a></sup> It was certified platinum in Australia in its first week by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA) and has since been certified double platinum for a shipment of 140,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Australiacert_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Australiacert-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>The record became the band's second number-one album in the United States in the week of 18 November 2012, and recorded the biggest first-week sales tally for an album by a boy band since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N%27Sync" title="N'Sync">N'Sync</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Celebrity_(album)" title="Celebrity (album)">Celebrity</a></i> (2001), and the third-largest debut sales week of 2012, behind <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Red_(Taylor_Swift_album)" title="Red (Taylor Swift album)">Red</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Babel_(album)" title="Babel (album)">Babel</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Mumford_%26_Sons" title="Mumford &amp; Sons">Mumford &amp; Sons</a>, with 540,000 copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USTMHdebut_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-USTMHdebut-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo1_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo1-81">[81]</a></sup> One Direction became the first group to bow atop the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with their first two albums since American girl group <a href="/wiki/Danity_Kane" title="Danity Kane">Danity Kane</a> entered with <i><a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Dollhouse_(album)" title="Welcome to the Dollhouse (album)">Welcome to the Dollhouse</a></i> in 2008 and their <a href="/wiki/Danity_Kane_(album)" title="Danity Kane (album)">self-titled debut</a> in 2006, the second act in 2012 to achieve two number-one albums within a 12-month period alongside <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>, and the first boy band in US chart history to land two number-one albums in a calendar year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USTMHdebut_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-USTMHdebut-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo1_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo1-81">[81]</a></sup> The album was certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) on 5 December 2012, denoting shipments of one million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-82">[82]</a></sup> It became their second album in 2012 to top the one million mark in US sales in the week of 16 December 2012, making them the first act to achieve the feat in a calendar year since 2009, and the first group or duo to achieve the feat since <a href="/wiki/Rascal_Flatts" title="Rascal Flatts">Rascal Flatts</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo2_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo2-83">[83]</a></sup> Their debut album and <i>Take Me Home</i> were the third and fifth best-selling albums of 2012 in the United States, respectively, making the band the first act to place two albums in the year-end top five in the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo3_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo3-84">[84]</a></sup> On 29 March 2015, it surpassed the 2 million thresold becoming their second album (after <i>Up All Night</i>) to sell over 2 million copies in the U.S. As of August 2015, the album has sold 2,020,000 copies in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Worldwide, according to <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music" title="Sony Music">Sony Music</a>, the album has sold over 5 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
